## Constraints
You must satisfy the following constraints:

3. **No commas** are allowed in the response. Use spaces or other punctuation as needed.
4. **The first word of each sentence must be the word "breakfast"**.

8. **Include specific words** (e.g., "possible") a certain number of times, as specified in the input.
9. **Use a generalizable strategy** if applicable, such as using a loop, formula, or algorithm to solve the problem, and explain it clearly.
10. **Ensure that all niche and domain-specific factual information** is included in the instruction, such as mathematical formulas, sports terminology, or programming concepts, to help the assistant understand the task in future interactions.

## Task Description

You are to write a Python function that analyzes a list of patients' ages and determines the percentage of patients who fall into specific age categories: infants (0-1 years), toddlers (2-4 years), children (5-12 years), and teenagers (13-18 years). The input will be a list of integers representing the ages of patients. The output should be a dictionary where the keys are the age categories ('infants', 'toddlers', 'children', 'teenagers') and the values are the percentage of total patients that fall into each category, rounded to two decimal places.

## Constraints and Requirements

1. The function must handle edge cases, such as an empty input list, by returning an empty dictionary.
2. The function must categorize each patient's age into the correct category based on the defined ranges.
3. The output must be a dictionary with the specified keys and percentage values, rounded to two decimal places.
4. The function must not include the keywords ['camera', 'green', 'revolution', 'watch'] in the response.
5. Include the keyword "reach" in the 14th sentence of the response, as the 12th word of that sentence.
6. The response must be written in clear, concise, and well-structured English, with code formatting where appropriate.
7. Provide a working example of the function with a sample input and expected output.
8. Ensure that the function is efficient and adheres to the constraints provided.

## Niche and Domain-Specific Information

- The function must accurately categorize patients based on age ranges, ensuring that each patient is counted in only one category.
- The percentage calculation must be based on the total number of patients in the input list.
- The function must be generalizable to any list of patient ages and must not assume any specific input format beyond a list of integers.
- The keyword "reach" must be included in the 14th sentence as the 12th word, without disrupting the flow of the explanation.
- The function must avoid any mention of the keywords 'camera', 'green', 'revolution', or 'watch'.

## Generalizable Strategy

- Use a dictionary to keep track of counts for each age category.
- Iterate through the input list and categorize each age into the appropriate range.
- Calculate the percentage for each category based on the total number of patients.
- Round the percentage to two decimal places.
- Return the result as a dictionary.
- Ensure that the function handles edge cases, such as an empty list.

Iteration 32: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instructions

## Task Overview
You are to generate a response that strictly adheres to a set of detailed formatting, content, and linguistic constraints. The task involves processing a given input and producing a structured, precise output that satisfies all specified requirements.

## Input Format
The input will consist of:
1. A **text prompt** or **task description**.
2. A **set of constraints** that specify formatting, content, and linguistic requirements for the output.
   - These constraints may include:
     - Specific word usage (e.g., a keyword must appear a certain number of times).
     - Language and case requirements (e.g., all text must be in English and in all capital letters).
     - Structural requirements (e.g., number of paragraphs, sentences, or words per sentence).
     - Content-based requirements (e.g., the first word of each sentence must be a specific word).
     - Formatting requirements (e.g., use of markdown dividers, code blocks, or other structural elements).

## Output Requirements
Your response must:
1. **Completely satisfy all constraints** provided in the input.
2. **Use English** and adhere to the specified case (e.g., all capital letters, all lowercase letters).
3. **Follow the exact structural format** (e.g., number of paragraphs, sentences, and words per sentence).
4. **Include specified keywords** with the required frequency.
5. **Avoid any text or formatting** not explicitly allowed by the constraints.
6. **Be concise and precise**, ensuring that no extra information is added or omitted.

## Domain-Specific Knowledge
- **Formatting**: Use markdown dividers (e.g., `* * *`) to separate paragraphs.
- **Linguistic Constraints**: Pay close attention to letter frequency, capitalization, and word usage.
- **Structural Constraints**: Ensure the output matches the exact number of paragraphs, sentences, and words per sentence.
- **Keyword Usage**: Include specified keywords with the required frequency.
- **Language**: Use only English and follow case rules (e.g., all caps, all lowercase).

## Generalizable Strategy
- Read and parse the input carefully to identify all constraints.
- Ensure that the output strictly follows the structure, formatting, and linguistic rules.
- Double-check for keyword frequency and content requirements.
- Avoid adding or omitting any information not explicitly required.
- Use clear, precise language to meet all constraints.

## Example
Input:
"Write a sentence in all capital letters. The letter 'S' should appear exactly 3 times. Include the keyword 'craft' once."

Output:
"THE CRAFT SUSTAINS THE STRENGTH OF THE SYSTEM."

## Your Task
Process the input and generate a response that satisfies all constraints. Make sure to include all required keywords, follow formatting rules, and adhere to linguistic and structural requirements.

Highlight at least two sections in your answer using markdown formatting, such as *highlighted section*. *highlighted section*  
**Function Overview:**  
The function should take a list of email addresses, extract the domain part from each email, and store them in a set to ensure uniqueness. It should then return the length of the set, which represents the number of unique domains.

*highlighted section*  
**Why Unique Domains Matter in Digital Marketing:**  
In Asian markets, where email is widely used for communication, identifying unique domains helps in understanding the geographic and demographic distribution of users. This information is crucial for targeted marketing campaigns, audience segmentation, and improving user engagement strategies.

**Key Considerations for the Function:**
- The function should normalize email addresses to lowercase to ensure consistency.
- It should split each email at the '@' symbol to extract the domain.
- Use a set to automatically handle duplicates and ensure only unique domains are counted.
- Include comments to explain each step of the function for clarity and maintainability.

**Function Implementation:**
```python
def count_unique_domains(email_list):
    """
    Calculate the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses.

    Parameters:
    email_list (list): A list of email addresses in lowercase format.

    Returns:
    int: The number of unique email domains.
    """
    # Initialize a set to store unique domains
    unique_domains = set()

    # Iterate over each email in the list
    for email in email_list:
        # Split the email at the '@' symbol to extract the domain
        domain = email.split('@')[-1]
        # Add the domain to the set
        unique_domains.add(domain)

    # Return the count of unique domains
    return len(unique_domains)
```

**Example Usage:**
```python
emails = [
    "user1@example.com",
    "user2@example.com",
    "user3@test.com",
    "user4@example.com"
]

print(count_unique_domains(emails))  # Output: 2
```

**Explanation:**  
The function processes each email by splitting it at the '@' symbol and extracting the domain. These domains are stored in a set, which automatically removes duplicates. The final count of unique domains is returned, providing a clear insight into the diversity of email sources.

**Additional Notes:**  
- This function assumes all email addresses are valid and in lowercase format. If validation is required, additional checks can be added.
- In digital marketing, especially in markets like China, India, and Southeast Asia, understanding email domains can provide insights into user behavior, regional trends, and campaign effectiveness.

Since the input is guaranteed to be in lowercase, the function does not need to handle case variations.

- **Input Format**: A list of strings, where each string is a valid email address in lowercase format (e.g., ["user@example.com", "admin@domain.co"]).

- **Data Analysis Use Case**: In digital marketing, especially in Asian markets where email is widely used for both personal and corporate communication, identifying unique email domains helps in understanding user demographics, geographic distribution, and engagement patterns. It also aids in detecting spam, assessing brand loyalty, and segmenting audiences for targeted campaigns.

7. Do not include any extra text or explanation beyond the function and its documentation.

1. **Email Format Handling:** Ensure the function validates that each email address is in the format `local-part@domain`, where the local part is a string of characters and the domain is a valid domain name. The function should not process invalid email addresses and should raise a `ValueError` if any invalid email is encountered.

2. **Case Sensitivity:** Although the function should process email addresses in lowercase format, it should not modify the input strings. Instead, it should extract the domain and convert it to lowercase before adding it to a set to ensure case-insensitive uniqueness.

3. **Performance Considerations:** Use a set to store unique domains because it provides average O(1) time complexity for insertions and lookups, making the function efficient even for large input lists.

4. **Domain Extraction:** The function should split each email address at the '@' character to isolate the domain. It should then strip any leading or trailing whitespace from the domain before adding it to the set.

*highlighted section*  
**Function Overview:**  
The function will process a list of email addresses, extract the domain part from each email, and store them in a set to automatically handle duplicates. Finally, it will return the size of the set, which represents the number of unique domains.

*highlighted section*  
**Usefulness in Digital Marketing (Asian Markets):**  
Identifying unique email domains is crucial for digital marketing in Asian markets, where email remains a dominant communication channel. Marketers can analyze domain distribution to understand user behavior, segment audiences, and target specific regions or demographics. This data helps in optimizing email campaigns, improving deliverability, and personalizing content for better engagement.

**Function Implementation:**

```python
def count_unique_domains(emails):
    """
    Calculate the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses.

    Parameters:
    emails (list of str): A list of email addresses in lowercase format.

    Returns:
    int: The number of unique email domains.

    Example:
    >>> count_unique_domains(["user1@example.com", "user2@example.com", "user3@test.com"])
    3
    """
    # Initialize an empty set to store unique domains
    unique_domains = set()

    # Iterate through each email address in the list
    for email in emails:
        # Split the email address into local part and domain part
        # The domain part is everything after the '@' symbol
        domain = email.split('@')[-1]
        # Add the domain to the set (sets automatically handle duplicates)
        unique_domains.add(domain)

    # Return the count of unique domains
    return len(unique_domains)
```

**Explanation:**  
The function `count_unique_domains` takes a list of email addresses as input. It processes each email by splitting it at the '@' symbol to extract the domain. These domains are stored in a set, which ensures that only unique domains are kept. Finally, the function returns the number of unique domains by getting the length of the set.

**Why This Matters in Digital Marketing:**  
In Asian markets, where email usage is widespread, analyzing unique email domains helps marketers understand user behavior, identify regional trends, and improve targeting strategies. This data can be used to refine marketing campaigns, enhance user segmentation, and improve overall engagement rates.

## Task Overview

You are to write a Python function that calculates the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. The function must validate each email address, extract the domain, and return the count of unique domains in lowercase format. The function should be well-documented, efficient, and handle various edge cases, including invalid emails and non-list inputs.

## Detailed Instructions

### 1. **Function Purpose and Scope**
Write a Python function named `count_unique_email_domains` that takes a list of email addresses as input and returns the number of unique email domains. The function should:
- Validate that each email is in the format `local-part@domain`.
- Extract the domain part from each valid email address.
- Convert the domain to lowercase to ensure case-insensitive uniqueness.
- Store the unique domains in a set for efficient lookup.
- Return the count of unique domains as an integer.

### 2. **Email Format Handling**
Ensure that the function validates each email address to confirm it is in the format `local-part@domain`. If an email is not valid, raise a `ValueError` with a descriptive message. For example, an email like `"user@domain"` is valid, but `"user@domain.com."` or `"user@.com"` is not.

### 3. **Case Sensitivity and Lowercasing**
Although the input emails are not modified, the domain part must be converted to lowercase before being added to the set to ensure case-insensitive uniqueness. For example, `"User@Domain.com"` and `"user@domain.com"` should both be treated as `"domain.com"`.

### 4. **Performance Considerations**
Use a set to store unique domains, as it provides average O(1) time complexity for insertions and lookups. This ensures that the function remains efficient even for large input lists.

### 5. **Domain Extraction**
Split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain. Strip any leading or trailing whitespace from the domain before adding it to the set. For example, `"user@  domain.com "` should be converted to `"domain.com"`.

### 6. **Use Case in Digital Marketing**
In digital marketing, especially in Asian markets where email is a primary communication channel, identifying unique email domains helps in:
- **Audience Segmentation**: Grouping users by their email domains allows for targeted marketing campaigns.
- **Email Deliverability**: Identifying domains with high engagement or low bounce rates can improve deliverability.
- **Customer Behavior Analysis**: Understanding the behavior of users from different domains can lead to more effective marketing strategies.

### 7. **Error Handling and Input Validation**
Ensure that the input is a list of strings. If the input is not a list or contains non-string elements, raise a `TypeError` with a clear message. For example, if the input is not a list, the function should raise an error like `"Input must be a list of strings."`

### 8. **Example Input and Output**
Provide a sample input list and the corresponding expected output to illustrate how the function should behave. For example:
```python
sample_emails = [
    "alice@example.com",
    "bob@example.com",
    "charlie@example.org",
    "dave@example.com"
]
# Expected Output: 3
```

### 9. **Documentation and Code Style**
- Include detailed comments in the code to explain the purpose of each section, the logic behind domain extraction, and the use of the set for uniqueness.
- Include a docstring that describes the function's parameters, return value, and any exceptions it may raise.
- Ensure the code adheres to PEP8 style guidelines, including proper indentation, spacing, and naming conventions.

### 10. **Testing and Robustness**
Outline how the function can be tested with different scenarios, such as:
- Edge cases (e.g., emails with special characters, empty strings, or invalid formats).
- Large datasets to ensure performance and memory efficiency.
- Invalid emails to confirm that `ValueError` is raised correctly.
- Non-list inputs to confirm that `TypeError` is raised.

## Task Description

You are to write a Python function that calculates the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. The function should process a list of strings, each representing a valid email address in lowercase format, and return an integer representing the count of unique domains. The domain is defined as the part of the email address that follows the '@' symbol. Since all input emails are in lowercase, the function does not need to handle case sensitivity.

The function should use Python's `set` data structure to efficiently store and count unique domains, leveraging the fact that sets automatically eliminate duplicates. The function should be well-documented with comments and adhere to PEP8 style guidelines, including proper indentation, spacing, and line breaks.

## Key Requirements

1. **Extracting the Domain**: The function should extract the domain by splitting the email string at the '@' character and taking the second part. This ensures that even if an email contains multiple '@' symbols (which is invalid, but the input is guaranteed to be valid), the correct domain is captured.

2. **Function Implementation**: The function should:
   - Accept a list of email addresses as input.
   - Process each email to extract the domain.
   - Store the domains in a set to automatically eliminate duplicates.
   - Return the count of unique domains.

3. **Documentation and Style**:
   - Include a docstring that explains the function's purpose, parameters, and return value.
   - Add inline comments to explain key steps in the code.
   - Ensure the code adheres to PEP8 style guidelines (e.g., proper spacing, indentation, line breaks).

4. **Contextual Explanation**:
   - Include a brief explanation of how the function works and why identifying unique email domains is useful for data analysis in digital marketing.
   - Specifically, highlight the importance of this analysis in Asian markets, where email usage is prevalent and often tied to corporate and personal identity. Mention how this helps in targeting the right audience for marketing campaigns and detecting potential fraud or spam.

## Additional Notes

- The function should be generalizable and work for any list of valid email addresses.
- The use of `set` is crucial for efficiently identifying and counting unique domains.
- The function should not modify the input list or perform any unnecessary operations.

## Example

Input:
```python
email_list = [
    "john.doe@example.com",
    "jane.smith@example.com",
    "alice.baker@example.com",
    "john.doe@example.com"
]

unique_domains = count_unique_domains(email_list)
print(unique_domains)  # Output: 1
```

## Niche and Domain-Specific Information

- **Digital Marketing Use Case**: Identifying unique email domains helps in analyzing user behavior, geographic distribution, and customer segmentation. In Asian markets, where email usage is prevalent and often tied to corporate and personal identity, this analysis is particularly useful for:
  - Targeting the right audience for marketing campaigns.
  - Detecting potential fraud or spam by identifying unusual or suspicious domains.
  - Understanding regional trends and preferences in email communication.

- **Email Validation Assumption**: The input is guaranteed to be valid, so the function does not need to handle invalid email formats (e.g., multiple '@' symbols, missing '@', etc.).

- **Performance Consideration**: Using a `set` is an efficient way to count unique domains, as it has an average time complexity of O(1) for insertions and lookups, making the function both time and space efficient.

## Generalizable Strategy

- The function follows a simple and efficient strategy:
  1. Iterate over each email in the input list.
  2. Split each email at the '@' character and extract the domain.
  3. Add the domain to a set.
  4. Return the size of the set, which represents the number of unique domains.

This approach ensures clarity, efficiency, and correctness, making it suitable for large datasets and real-world applications.

Iteration 106: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction: Write a Python Function to Count Unique Email Domains

## Task Description

You are to write a Python function that calculates the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. The function should process a list of strings, each representing a valid email address in lowercase format, and return an integer representing the count of unique domains. The domain is defined as the part of the email address that follows the '@' symbol.

## Key Requirements

1. **Input**: A list of strings, where each string is a valid email address in lowercase format.
2. **Output**: An integer representing the count of unique email domains.
3. **Domain Extraction**: Extract the domain by splitting the email string at the '@' character and taking the second part. This ensures that even if an email contains multiple '@' symbols (which is invalid, but the input is guaranteed to be valid), the correct domain is captured.
4. **Efficiency**: Use Python's `set` data structure to store and count unique domains, leveraging the fact that sets automatically eliminate duplicates.
5. **Documentation**: Include detailed comments and adhere to PEP8 style guidelines, including proper indentation, spacing, and line breaks.
6. **Contextual Explanation**: Include a brief explanation of how the function works and why identifying unique email domains is useful for data analysis in digital marketing, especially in Asian markets.

## Additional Notes

- The function should be well-documented with comments explaining each step.
- The function should be named in a clear and descriptive manner (e.g., `count_unique_domains`).
- The function should handle edge cases, such as empty input lists, and return 0 in such cases.
- The function should not modify the input list and should work with any valid list of email addresses.

## Niche and Domain-Specific Information

- **Digital Marketing Use Case**: Identifying unique email domains is particularly useful in digital marketing for analyzing user behavior, geographic distribution, and customer segmentation. In Asian markets, where email usage is prevalent and often tied to corporate and personal identity, this analysis helps in targeting the right audience for marketing campaigns and detecting potential fraud or spam.
- **Domain Extraction Strategy**: The function uses a simple and efficient method to extract domains by splitting the email string at the '@' symbol. This is reliable for valid email addresses and ensures that the correct domain is captured.

## Generalizable Strategy

- The function uses a `set` to store unique domains, which is an efficient way to eliminate duplicates.
- The function processes each email address in the list by splitting the string at the '@' symbol and taking the second part.
- The function returns the length of the set, which gives the count of unique domains.

## Example

Input:
```python
emails = [
    "user1@example.com",
    "user2@example.com",
    "user3@test.com",
    "user4@example.com"
]
```

Output:
```python
2  # 'example.com' and 'test.com'
```
